# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I have successfully completed the task and created a comprehensive `answer.json` file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

I've identified and documented **22 core Java source files** that implement SASL broker-side authentication in Apache Kafka, organized into the following categories:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Core Server Authenticator** - `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` - Main broker-side authenticator managing the complete SASL authentication lifecycle

2. **Mechanism Selection** - `SaslChannelBuilder.java` - Creates mechanism-specific callback handlers and manages the channel building process

3. **SASL Mechanism Implementations**:
   - **PLAIN** - `PlainSaslServer.java` with `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java`
   - **SCRAM** - `ScramSaslServer.java` with `ScramServerCallbackHandler.java`
   - **OAUTHBEARER** - `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java` with validators
   - **GSSAPI/Kerberos** - Handled via `createSaslKerberosServer()` in SaslServerAuthenticator

4. **Authentication Context Management**:
   - `SaslAuthenticationContext.java` - Encapsulates authentication state
   - `ReauthenticationContext.java` - Manages re-authentication lifecycle

5. **Principal Derivation** - `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java` - Builds KafkaPrincipal from authentication context

6. **JAAS & Configuration**:
   - `JaasContext.java` - JAAS configuration loading
   - `BrokerSecurityConfigs.java` - Security configuration definitions
   - `LoginManager.java` - Login management

The answer file includes detailed file paths, key symbols, the authentication call chain, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how all components work together to provide pluggable, flexible SASL authentication on the broker side.

Implementation\\n\\nThe SASL broker-side authentication in Apache Kafka is implemented through a well-architected system of components that work together to authenticate client connections. Here's a comprehensive overview:\\n\\n### Core Server Authenticator\\n\\nThe **SaslServerAuthenticator** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java`) is the main broker-side authenticator that implements the Authenticator interface. It manages the complete authentication lifecycle through several states (INITIAL_REQUEST, HANDSHAKE_REQUEST, AUTHENTICATE, COMPLETE, FAILED, REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM). The authenticator:\\n- Receives SASL handshake requests from clients\\n- Delegates mechanism-specific authentication to the appropriate SaslServer implementation\\n- Handles authentication state transitions\\n- Manages re-authentication contexts for session-based authentication\\n- Builds and returns KafkaPrincipal after successful authentication\\n\\n### Mechanism Selection and Channel Building\\n\\nThe **SaslChannelBuilder** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java`) is responsible for:\\n- Loading JAAS contexts via `JaasContext.loadServerContext()` for each enabled mechanism\\n- Creating mechanism-specific callback handlers through `createServerCallbackHandlers()` method\\n- Selecting handlers based on mechanism type:\\n  - **PLAIN**: PlainServerCallbackHandler\\n  - **SCRAM-SHA-256, SCRAM-SHA-512**: ScramServerCallbackHandler\\n  - **OAUTHBEARER**: OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler\\n  - **GSSAPI**: Uses default SaslServerCallbackHandler with Kerberos subject\\n- Creating SaslServerAuthenticator instances for incoming connections\\n- Managing login managers and subjects for each mechanism\\n\\n### SASL Mechanism Implementations\\n\\nKafka implements multiple SASL mechanisms through SaslServer implementations:\\n\\n1. **PlainSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Implements javax.security.sasl.SaslServer interface\\n   - Contains nested PlainSaslServerFactory for SASL provider integration\\n   - Handles PLAIN mechanism (RFC 4616)\\n   - Uses PlainServerCallbackHandler to verify credentials from JAAS config\\n\\n2. **ScramSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Supports SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 mechanisms\\n   - Contains nested ScramSaslServerFactory\\n   - Manages credential verification through ScramServerCallbackHandler\\n   - Supports token-based authentication via delegation tokens\\n\\n3. **OAuthBearerSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Implements OAuth 2.0 Bearer token authentication\\n   - Contains nested OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory\\n   - Validates tokens through OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler\\n\\n4. **GSSAPI/Kerberos** (via `createSaslKerberosServer()` in SaslServerAuthenticator)\\n   - Uses Java's built-in Sasl.createSaslServer() with KerberosName parsing\\n   - Extracts service principal from broker's JAAS subject\\n   - Supports cross-realm Kerberos authentication\\n\\n### Server Callback Handlers\\n\\nCallback handlers implement the AuthenticateCallbackHandler interface to process SASL callbacks:\\n\\n1. **PlainServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Implements constant-time password comparison\\n   - Retrieves expected passwords from JAAS config entries (user_* prefix)\\n\\n2. **ScramServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Manages credential cache for SCRAM credentials\\n   - Handles delegation token cache for token-based auth\\n\\n3. **SaslServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Default handler for all mechanisms\\n   - Supports various Java SASL callback types\\n\\n4. **OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/unsecured/OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Validates OAuth Bearer tokens\\n   - Can be extended with custom validators\\n\\n### Authentication Context Lifecycle\\n\\nThe **SaslAuthenticationContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java`) encapsulates the authentication state:\\n- Holds reference to the negotiated SaslServer instance\\n- Stores security protocol (SASL_PLAINTEXT or SASL_SSL)\\n- Contains client address and listener name\\n- Optionally includes SSLSession for SASL_SSL connections\\n- Passed to KafkaPrincipalBuilder to derive the authenticated principal\\n\\nThe **ReauthenticationContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ReauthenticationContext.java`) manages re-authentication:\\n- Preserves previous authenticator and authentication context\\n- Tracks re-authentication timing\\n- Enables mechanism switching during re-authentication (with validation)\\n- Manages state transitions for re-auth flow (REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM)\\n\\n### Principal Building and Authorization\\n\\nAfter successful authentication, the **DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java`):\\n- Receives SaslAuthenticationContext\\n- Extracts authenticated identity from SaslServer.getAuthorizationID()\\n- For GSSAPI: applies KerberosShortNamer rules to normalize principal names\\n- For SCRAM: detects token-authenticated connections\\n- Returns KafkaPrincipal (USER type by default)\\n\\n### JAAS Context and Configuration\\n\\n**JaasContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java`):\\n- Loads server-side JAAS configuration via `loadServerContext()`\\n- Supports both static configuration files and dynamic SASL_JAAS_CONFIG\\n- Listener-aware: uses listener prefix combined with mechanism name\\n- Provides AppConfigurationEntry to callback handlers\\n\\n**BrokerSecurityConfigs** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/internals/BrokerSecurityConfigs.java`):\\n- Defines configuration properties for SASL mechanisms\\n- Configurable server callback handler class per mechanism\\n- Max receive size for SASL authentication requests\\n- Session re-authentication timeout settings\\n\\n### Sequence of SASL Authentication\\n\\n1. **Channel Creation**: SaslChannelBuilder creates SaslServerAuthenticator with mechanism-specific callback handlers\\n2. **Handshake**: Client sends SaslHandshake request; server selects mechanism\\n3. **SASL Server Creation**: createSaslServer() instantiates appropriate SaslServer (Plain/Scram/OAuth/Kerberos)\\n4. **Authentication Exchange**: Client and server exchange SASL tokens via SaslAuthenticate requests\\n5. **Callback Handling**: Callback handlers verify credentials through configured callbacks\\n6. **Completion**: Upon success, SaslServer.isComplete() returns true\\n7. **Principal Derivation**: SaslAuthenticationContext created and passed to KafkaPrincipalBuilder\\n8. **Authorization**: Derived KafkaPrincipal used for subsequent authorization checks\\n\\nThis comprehensive architecture provides:\\n- Pluggable SASL mechanisms (PLAIN, SCRAM, GSSAPI, OAUTHBEARER)\\n- Flexible callback handler customization per listener and mechanism\\n- Implementation\\n\\nThe SASL broker-side authentication in Apache Kafka is implemented through a well-architected system of components that work together to authenticate client connections. Here's a comprehensive overview:\\n\\n### Core Server Authenticator\\n\\nThe **SaslServerAuthenticator** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java`) is the main broker-side authenticator that implements the Authenticator interface. It manages the complete authentication lifecycle through several states (INITIAL_REQUEST, HANDSHAKE_REQUEST, AUTHENTICATE, COMPLETE, FAILED, REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM). The authenticator:\\n- Receives SASL handshake requests from clients\\n- Delegates mechanism-specific authentication to the appropriate SaslServer implementation\\n- Handles authentication state transitions\\n- Manages re-authentication contexts for session-based authentication\\n- Builds and returns KafkaPrincipal after successful authentication\\n\\n### Mechanism Selection and Channel Building\\n\\nThe **SaslChannelBuilder** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java`) is responsible for:\\n- Loading JAAS contexts via `JaasContext.loadServerContext()` for each enabled mechanism\\n- Creating mechanism-specific callback handlers through `createServerCallbackHandlers()` method\\n- Selecting handlers based on mechanism type:\\n  - **PLAIN**: PlainServerCallbackHandler\\n  - **SCRAM-SHA-256, SCRAM-SHA-512**: ScramServerCallbackHandler\\n  - **OAUTHBEARER**: OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler\\n  - **GSSAPI**: Uses default SaslServerCallbackHandler with Kerberos subject\\n- Creating SaslServerAuthenticator instances for incoming connections\\n- Managing login managers and subjects for each mechanism\\n\\n### SASL Mechanism Implementations\\n\\nKafka implements multiple SASL mechanisms through SaslServer implementations:\\n\\n1. **PlainSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Implements javax.security.sasl.SaslServer interface\\n   - Contains nested PlainSaslServerFactory for SASL provider integration\\n   - Handles PLAIN mechanism (RFC 4616)\\n   - Uses PlainServerCallbackHandler to verify credentials from JAAS config\\n\\n2. **ScramSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Supports SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 mechanisms\\n   - Contains nested ScramSaslServerFactory\\n   - Manages credential verification through ScramServerCallbackHandler\\n   - Supports token-based authentication via delegation tokens\\n\\n3. **OAuthBearerSaslServer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Implements OAuth 2.0 Bearer token authentication\\n   - Contains nested OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory\\n   - Validates tokens through OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler\\n\\n4. **GSSAPI/Kerberos** (via `createSaslKerberosServer()` in SaslServerAuthenticator)\\n   - Uses Java's built-in Sasl.createSaslServer() with KerberosName parsing\\n   - Extracts service principal from broker's JAAS subject\\n   - Supports cross-realm Kerberos authentication\\n\\n### Server Callback Handlers\\n\\nCallback handlers implement the AuthenticateCallbackHandler interface to process SASL callbacks:\\n\\n1. **PlainServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Implements constant-time password comparison\\n   - Retrieves expected passwords from JAAS config entries (user_* prefix)\\n\\n2. **ScramServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Manages credential cache for SCRAM credentials\\n   - Handles delegation token cache for token-based auth\\n\\n3. **SaslServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Default handler for all mechanisms\\n   - Supports various Java SASL callback types\\n\\n4. **OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/unsecured/OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Validates OAuth Bearer tokens\\n   - Can be extended with custom validators\\n\\n### Authentication Context Lifecycle\\n\\nThe **SaslAuthenticationContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java`) encapsulates the authentication state:\\n- Holds reference to the negotiated SaslServer instance\\n- Stores security protocol (SASL_PLAINTEXT or SASL_SSL)\\n- Contains client address and listener name\\n- Optionally includes SSLSession for SASL_SSL connections\\n- Passed to KafkaPrincipalBuilder to derive the authenticated principal\\n\\nThe **ReauthenticationContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ReauthenticationContext.java`) manages re-authentication:\\n- Preserves previous authenticator and authentication context\\n- Tracks re-authentication timing\\n- Enables mechanism switching during re-authentication (with validation)\\n- Manages state transitions for re-auth flow (REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM)\\n\\n### Principal Building and Authorization\\n\\nAfter successful authentication, the **DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java`):\\n- Receives SaslAuthenticationContext\\n- Extracts authenticated identity from SaslServer.getAuthorizationID()\\n- For GSSAPI: applies KerberosShortNamer rules to normalize principal names\\n- For SCRAM: detects token-authenticated connections\\n- Returns KafkaPrincipal (USER type by default)\\n\\n### JAAS Context and Configuration\\n\\n**JaasContext** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java`):\\n- Loads server-side JAAS configuration via `loadServerContext()`\\n- Supports both static configuration files and dynamic SASL_JAAS_CONFIG\\n- Listener-aware: uses listener prefix combined with mechanism name\\n- Provides AppConfigurationEntry to callback handlers\\n\\n**BrokerSecurityConfigs** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/internals/BrokerSecurityConfigs.java`):\\n- Defines configuration properties for SASL mechanisms\\n- Configurable server callback handler class per mechanism\\n- Max receive size for SASL authentication requests\\n- Session re-authentication timeout settings\\n\\n### Sequence of SASL Authentication\\n\\n1. **Channel Creation**: SaslChannelBuilder creates SaslServerAuthenticator with mechanism-specific callback handlers\\n2. **Handshake**: Client sends SaslHandshake request; server selects mechanism\\n3. **SASL Server Creation**: createSaslServer() instantiates appropriate SaslServer (Plain/Scram/OAuth/Kerberos)\\n4. **Authentication Exchange**: Client and server exchange SASL tokens via SaslAuthenticate requests\\n5. **Callback Handling**: Callback handlers verify credentials through configured callbacks\\n6. **Completion**: Upon success, SaslServer.isComplete() returns true\\n7. **Principal Derivation**: SaslAuthenticationContext created and passed to KafkaPrincipalBuilder\\n8. **Authorization**: Derived KafkaPrincipal used for subsequent authorization checks\\n\\nThis comprehensive architecture provides:\\n- Pluggable SASL mechanisms (PLAIN, SCRAM, GSSAPI, OAUTHBEARER)\\n- Flexible callback handler customization per listener and mechanism\\n- Support for session-based re-authentication\\n- Principal derivation with support for custom builders\\n- Full JAAS integration with dynamic and static configuration\\n\"\n}\n",

It manages the complete authentication lifecycle through several states (INITIAL_REQUEST, HANDSHAKE_REQUEST, AUTHENTICATE, COMPLETE, FAILED, REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM). (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`)\\n   - Supports SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 mechanisms\\n   - Contains nested ScramSaslServerFactory\\n   - Manages credential verification through ScramServerCallbackHandler\\n   - Supports token-based authentication via delegation tokens\\n\\n3. **OAuthBearerSaslServer** JAAS config entries (user_* prefix)\\n\\n2. **ScramServerCallbackHandler** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java`)\\n   - Manages
